
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Rewrite the polynomial expression in terms of symmetric sums or simpler algebraic forms involving a, b, and c.'}, {'objective': 'Use the condition a + b + c = 300 to relate and simplify the polynomial equation.'}, {'objective': 'Determine all nonnegative integer triples (a,b,c) satisfying both the sum condition and the polynomial equation.'}, {'objective': 'Count the number of such triples (a,b,c) that meet both conditions.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- Variables: Nonnegative integers a, b, c.
- Constraints:
  * Linear sum: a + b + c = 300.
  * Polynomial condition: a^2b + a^2c + b^2a + b^2c + c^2a + c^2b = 6,000,000.
- The polynomial is symmetric in a, b, c and involves terms of degree 3 (since each term is quadratic in one variable and linear in another).

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The sum constraint restricts the triples to lie on the plane a + b + c = 300 in the nonnegative integer lattice.
- The polynomial condition is a symmetric homogeneous expression of degree 3, combining terms like a^2b and a^2c, which can be grouped or rewritten using symmetric sums.
- The polynomial can be expressed as a sum over permutations of variables, indicating symmetry and potential for simplification using symmetric polynomial identities.
- The constraints together define a discrete set of points (a,b,c) in the positive octant intersecting a plane and a nonlinear surface.
- The problem likely requires understanding how the polynomial relates to the sum and how these conditions restrict the possible triples.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- Primary domain: Combinatorics (counting integer solutions under constraints).
- Secondary domains: Algebra (symmetric polynomials), Number Theory (integer solutions), and possibly Discrete Geometry.
- Concepts involved: Integer partitions, symmetric polynomial identities, Diophantine equations.
- Applications: Problems of this type appear in mathematical competitions, enumerative combinatorics, and algebraic problem solving.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The polynomial expression is symmetric but not immediately standard; rewriting or simplification might be needed.
- The problem does not specify if permutations of (a,b,c) are considered distinct or not; however, since (a,b,c) are triples, order likely matters.
- Potential complexity arises from the nonlinear polynomial constraint combined with the linear sum.
- The size of numbers (sum 300, polynomial value 6,000,000) suggests that direct enumeration is impractical.
- No explicit domain restrictions beyond nonnegativity; no mention of upper bounds other than sum.
- The problem assumes familiarity with symmetric polynomial manipulation and counting integer solutions under nonlinear constraints.

    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_sc_instruction_0_1 = "Sub-task 0_1: Rewrite and simplify the polynomial expression a^2b + a^2c + b^2a + b^2c + c^2a + c^2b using symmetric polynomial identities and express it in terms of elementary symmetric sums or other simpler symmetric expressions."
    cot_sc_agents_0_1 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.5) for _ in range(self.max_sc)]
    possible_answers_0_1 = []
    possible_thinkings_0_1 = []
    subtask_desc_0_1 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_0_1",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_0_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(self.max_sc):
        thinking, answer = await cot_sc_agents_0_1[i]([taskInfo], cot_sc_instruction_0_1, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_sc_agents_0_1[i].id}, simplifying polynomial, thinking: {thinking.content}; answer: {answer.content}")
        possible_answers_0_1.append(answer)
        possible_thinkings_0_1.append(thinking)
    final_decision_agent_0_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking_0_1, answer_0_1 = await final_decision_agent_0_1([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_0_1 + possible_answers_0_1, "Sub-task 0_1: Synthesize and choose the most consistent simplification of the polynomial expression.", is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 0_1 output: thinking - {thinking_0_1.content}; answer - {answer_0_1.content}")
    subtask_desc_0_1['response'] = {"thinking": thinking_0_1, "answer": answer_0_1}

async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_sc_instruction_0_1 = (
        "Sub-task 0_1: Rewrite and simplify the polynomial expression a^2b + a^2c + b^2a + b^2c + c^2a + c^2b "
        "using symmetric polynomial identities. Express it in terms of elementary symmetric sums or other simpler symmetric expressions to reduce complexity and facilitate further analysis."
    )
    cot_sc_agents_0_1 = [
        LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.5)
        for _ in range(self.max_sc)
    ]
    possible_answers_0_1 = []
    possible_thinkings_0_1 = []
    subtask_desc_0_1 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_0_1",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_0_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(self.max_sc):
        thinking, answer = await cot_sc_agents_0_1[i]([taskInfo], cot_sc_instruction_0_1, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_sc_agents_0_1[i].id}, simplifying polynomial, thinking: {thinking.content}; answer: {answer.content}")
        possible_thinkings_0_1.append(thinking)
        possible_answers_0_1.append(answer)
    final_decision_agent_0_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
